        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>With just 27 Triple-A plate appearances to his name, DeShields wasn't supposed to find himself with a starting job in the outfield this year. But injuries and poor play by the incumbents in Texas helped vault the speedy DeShields into an everyday role. He figures to open the year as the team's starting centerfielder and leadoff hitter, though his job may not be so safe given his weak defense. However, if he does manage to stick around, he has some upside in both the power and speed categories. Surely he could nudge that microscopic 2% home run per flyball rate up, and my gosh has he shown blazing speed during his time in the minors. He stole 101 (!!!!) bases back in 2012, and then followed up with 50+ the next two years. If given the green light, you would imagine there's room for major growth from the 25 steals he recorded last year. (<a href="http://www.projectingx.com/" target="_blank">Mike Podhorzer</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Set to open the season as the everyday leadoff guy in Texas, DeShields has the potential to increase both his power and speed numbers, perhaps significantly. No, he won't hit 20 homers, but he could threaten double digits, and when paired with the potential for 40+ steals, he could prove quite valuable.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>DeShields entered the 2016 season after a promising 2015 campaign that highlighted his speed and his ability to get on base. Sadly, he couldn't keep it up, as his walk rate fell, strikeout rate spiked, and BABIP collapsed. As is often the case, he was probably a bit lucky in 2015, while his luck overcorrected in 2016 and he suffered from some poor fortune. That means he'll head into 2017 as a reserve outfielder at best. But given his speed, he's the type of guy to speculate on during dollar days or reserve round of your AL-Only auction or draft. This is especially true in leagues that count OBP instead of average, where DeShields is worth more.Â (<a href="http://www.projectingx.com/" target="_blank">Mike Podhorzer</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Yet another intriguing sleeper that didn't pan out in 2016, his offensive ineptitude cost him his starting job and even got him sent back to the farm. But with his speed, he's a worthy roster filler with the hopes injuries vault him back into the lineup.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>
